## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillations / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where the equation of motion includes nonlinear restoring forces (functions of x), nonlinear damping (functions of v), and possibly time-dependent driving terms. The relationship dv/dt = f(x, v, t) represents Newton's second law with various nonlinear force contributions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (linear oscillator with sinusoidal driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic-cubic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Mathieu-type parametric: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (parametric excitation)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (position-dependent stiffness)
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v + c4 * v**3 (combined nonlinearities)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium, while even powers (x**2) break symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms (c*v, c*v**3, c*v*x**2) represent energy dissipation or injection — sign of coefficient determines damping vs. self-excitation
- Products of position and velocity (x*v, x**2*v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of van der Pol-type oscillators
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic driving forces, leading to resonance phenomena
- Cubic position terms (x**3) with same sign as linear term indicate hardening spring; opposite sign indicates softening spring
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is conserved or dissipated monotonically
- Parametric terms like x*cos(c*t) indicate time-varying stiffness rather than direct forcing, leading to parametric resonance
- Negative linear damping (positive coefficient on v) combined with cubic velocity saturation (negative v**3) indicates limit cycle behavior
